             fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">To improve tolerability, it is recommended to begin treatment with a low initial dose with subsequent gradual increases. In the first week, Acme Product 30 mg is taken once daily (1 tablet in the evening). In the second week, Acme Product 30 mg is taken twice daily (1 tablet in the morning and 1 in the evening). In the third week, Acme Product 30 mg is taken three times daily (1 tablet in the morning, 1 at midday, and 1 in the evening). From the fourth week, treatment is switched to only 1 tablet of Acme Product 120 mg in the evening. This dose is then increased by 1 Acme Product 120 mg tablet per week at different times of day for the subsequent 5 weeks, as shown in the table below. The maximum daily dose allowed is 720 mg (3 x 2 tablets of Acme Product 120 mg).</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <table border=\"0\" cellpadding=\"0\" cellspacing=\"0\" width=\"100%\" style=\"width:100.0%;border-collapse:collapse\" class=\"Tablanormal\">\n                                            <tr>\n                                                <td width=\"10%\" style=\"width:10.42%;border:solid windowtext 1.0pt; Based on the pharmacology of dimethyl fumarate, a need for dose adjustment in the elderly is not expected.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <i>\n                                                <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Renal impairment</span>\n                                            </i>\n                 <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product has not been studied in patients with severe renal impairment, and use of Acme Product is contraindicated in these patients (see section            fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:  0in;margin-left:28.35pt;text-indent:-28.35pt;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"Prrafodelista\">\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Calibri&quot;,sans-serif\" lang=\"EN-GB\">‒</span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">Hypersensitivity to the active substance or to any of the excipients listed in section 6.1.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:  0in;margin-left:28.35pt;text-indent:-28.35pt\" class=\"Prrafodelista\">\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Calibri&quot;,sans-serif\" lang=\"EN-GB\">‒</span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">Severe gastrointestinal disorders.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;margin-bottom:  0in;margin-left:28.35pt;text-indent:-28.35pt\" class=\"Prrafodelista\">\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Calibri&quot;,sans-serif\" lang=\"EN-GB\">‒</span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">Severe hepatic or renal impairment.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-top:0in;margin-right:0in;  margin-bottom:0in;margin-left:28.35pt;text-indent:-28.35pt\" class=\"PrrafodelistaCxSpLast\">\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;font-family:&quot;Calibri&quot;,sans-serif\" lang=\"EN-GB\">‒</span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">Pregnancy and breast-feeding.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                </div>"         ]       ], [
         fhir:index 3;
         fhir:Element.id [ fhir:value "52fbef30-5b80-4ece-8b05-772b36916b89" ];
         fhir:Composition.section.title [ fhir:value "4.4     Special warnings and precautions for use" ];
         fhir:Composition.section.code [
           fhir:CodeableConcept.coding [
             fhir:index 0;
             fhir:Coding.system [ fhir:value "http://spor.ema.europa.eu/v1/example-sections" ];
             fhir:Coding.code [ fhir:value "17" ];
             fhir:Coding.display [ fhir:value "4.4 Special warnings and precautions for use" ]           ]         ];
         fhir:Composition.section.text [
           fhir:Narrative.status [ fhir:value "additional" ];
           fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Haematology</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product may decrease leukocyte and lymphocyte counts (see section 4.8). It has not been studied in patients with pre-existing low leukocyte or lymphocyte counts.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Before treatment</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Prior to initiating treatment with </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product, a current complete blood count (including differential blood count and platelet count) should be available. Treatment should not be initiated if</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">leukopenia</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">below 3.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L,\n                                        </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">lymphopenia below </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">1.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L\n                                        </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">or other pathological results are identified.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">During treatment</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">During treatment a complete blood count with differential should be performed every 3 months. Action is needed in the following circumstances:</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" id=\"3de69782-1a9a-4ad4-895d-e8578e4f0ffa\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <i>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Leukopenia:</span>\n                                    </i>\n                                    <none/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" id=\"3de69782-1a9a-4ad4-895d-e8578e4f0ffa\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">If a marked decrease in the total number of white blood cells isfound, the situation should be monitored carefully and treatment withAcme Product should be discontinued at levels below 3.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L.\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" id=\"ca0bf9c4-c58f-40b6-8adc-462ad91e700d\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <i>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Lymphopenia:</span>\n                                    </i>\n                                    <none/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" id=\"ca0bf9c4-c58f-40b6-8adc-462ad91e700d\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">If the lymphocyte count falls below 1.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L\n                                        </span>\n                                        <span style=\"color:black\" lang=\"EN-GB\">but is ≥0.7 x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L\n                                        </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">, blood monitoring should be performed monthly until levels returnto 1.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L or higher for two consecutive blood tests at whichpoint monitoring can again be performed every 3 months.\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">If the\nlymphocyte count falls below 0.7x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L, the blood test must be\nrepeated and if the levels are confirmed to be below 0.7x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L, then\ntreatment must be stopped immediately. Patients developing lymphopenia should\nbe monitored after stopping treatment until their lymphocyte count has returned\nto the normal range (see section 4.8).\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Other haematological disorders</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Therapy should be discontinued and caution is advised if other pathological results occur. In any case blood counts should be monitored until values have returned to the normal range.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Infections</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product is an immunomodulator and may affect the way the immune system responds to infection. For p</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">atients with pre‑existing infections of clinical relevance, the physician should decide if treatment with Acme Product should only be initiated once the infection has resolved. If a patient develops an infection during treatment with Acme Product, suspension of treatment should be considered and the benefits and risks should be reassessed prior to re-initiation of therapy. Patients receiving Acme Product should be instructed to report symptoms of infection to a physician.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Opportunistic infections/progressive multifocal leukoencephalopathy (PML)</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Cases of opportunistic infections, particularly of progressive multifocal leukoencephalopathy (PML) have been reported with other dimethyl fumarate-containing products (see section 4.8). PML is an opportunistic infection caused by the John‑Cunningham virus (JCV) that can be fatal or cause severe disabilities. PML is probably caused by a combination of factors.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">A previous infection with JCV is considered a prerequisite for the development of PML. Risk factors can include previous immunosuppressive treatment and the existence of certain concomitant disorders (such as some autoimmune disorders or malignant haematological conditions). A modified or weakened immune system as well as genetic or environmental factors can also constitute risk factors.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Persistent moderate or severe lymphopenia during treatment with dimethyl fumarate is also considered a risk factor for PML. Patients who develop lymphopenia should be monitored for signs and symptoms of opportunistic infections, particularly for symptoms indicative of PML. Typical symptoms associated with PML are diverse, become worse over days to weeks and include progressive weakness on one side of the body or clumsiness of limbs, disturbance of vision and changes in thinking, memory and orientation leading to confusion and personality changes. If PML is suspected, treatment with Acme Product should be stopped immediately and further appropriate neurological and radiological examinations performed.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Prior </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">and concomitant </span>\n                                        </u>\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">treatment with immunosuppressive or immunomodulating therapies</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Limited</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">data are available on the efficacy and safety of Acme Product in patients who have been previously treated with other immunosuppressive or immunomodulating therapies. When switching patients from such therapies to Acme Product, the half-life and mode of action of the other therapy should be considered in order to avoid additive effects on the immune system.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">No data are available on the efficacy and safety of Acme Product when taken concomitantly with other immunosuppressive or immunomodulating therapies (see section 4.5).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Pre‑existing gastrointestinal disease</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"page-break-after:avoid;text-autospace:ideograph-numeric ideograph-other\" class=\"Default\">\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;color:windowtext\" lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product has not been studied in patients with pre-existing gastrointestinal disease.</span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product is contraindicated in patients with severe </span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">gastrointestinal disease </span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;color:windowtext\" lang=\"EN-GB\">(see sections 4.3)</span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt\" lang=\"EN-GB\">. Gastrointestinal tolerability can be improved by following the </span>\n                                        <span style=\"font-size:11.0pt;color:windowtext\" lang=\"EN-GB\">dose titration schedule on initiating Acme Product treatment and by taking Acme Product with food (see sections 4.2 and 4.8).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p class=\"Default\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Renal function</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Since renal elimination plays a minor role in the clearance of Acme Product from plasma, it is unlikely that renal impairment would affect the pharmacokinetic characteristics, and so a need for dose adjustment in patients with mild to moderate renal impairment is not expected (see sections 4.2 and 5.2).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">During the Phase III placebo-controlled clinical trial, renal function was not seen to deteriorate during therapy across treatment groups. However, Acme Product has not been studied in patients with severe renal impairment, and some cases of renal toxicity have been reported during post-marketing surveillance with fumaric acid esters. Hence, Acme Product is contraindicated in patients with severe renal impairment (see section 4.3).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Renal function (e.g. creatinine, blood urea nitrogen and urinalysis) should be checked prior to initiation of treatment and every 3 months thereafter. In the event of a clinically relevant change in renal function, particularly in the absence of alternative explanations, consideration should be given to dosage reduction or treatment discontinuation.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Fanconi syndrome</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Early diagnosis of Fanconi syndrome and discontinuation of Acme Product treatment are important to prevent the onset of renal impairment and osteomalacia, as the syndrome is usually reversible. The most important signs are: proteinuria, glucosuria (with normal blood sugar levels), hyperaminoaciduria and phosphaturia (possibly concurrent with hypophosphatemia). Progression might involve symptoms such as polyuria, polydipsia and proximal muscle weakness. In rare cases hypophosphataemic osteomalacia with non-localised bone pain, elevated alkaline phosphatase in serum and stress fractures may occur. Importantly, Fanconi syndrome can occur without elevated creatinine levels or low glomerular filtration rate. In case of unclear symptoms Fanconi syndrome should be considered and appropriate examinations should be performed.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Hepatic function</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product has not been studied in patients with severe hepatic impairment and is contraindicated in these patients (see section 4.3). </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">It is recommended to monitor hepatic function (SGOT, SGPT, gamma‑GT, AP) prior to initiation of treatment and every 3 months thereafter, since elevation of hepatic enzymes has been observed in some patients in the Phase III study. In the event of a clinically relevant change in hepatic parameters, particularly in the absence of alternative explanations, consideration should be given to dose reduction or treatment discontinuation.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Flushing</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Patients should be made aware that they are likely to experience flushing in the first few weeks of taking Acme Product (see section 4.8).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Lactose</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product contains lactose. Patients with rare hereditary problems of galactose intolerance, total lactase deficiency or glucose-galactose malabsorption should not take this medicine.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                </div>"         ]       ], [

                          <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">No interaction studies have been performed.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product should </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">be used cautiously in combination </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">with other</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">systemic antipsoriatic therapy (e.g. methotrexate, retinoids, psoralens, ciclosporin, immunosuppressants or cytostatics) (see section 4.4). </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">During treatment with Acme Product, simultaneous use of other fumaric acid derivatives (topical or systemic) should be avoided.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Concurrent therapy with nephrotoxic substances (e.g. methotrexate, ciclosporin, aminoglycosides, diuretics, NSAIDs or lithium) may increase the potential for renal adverse reactions (e.g. proteinuria) in patients taking Acme Product.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">In cases of severe or prolonged diarrhoea during treatment with Acme Product, absorption of other medicinal products may be affected. Caution should be exercised when prescribing medicinal products with a narrow therapeutic index that require absorption in the intestinal tract.</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The efficacy of oral contraceptives may be reduced and the use of an alternative barrier contraceptive method is recommended to prevent possible failure of contraception (see the prescribing information of the oral contraceptive).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Consumption of large quantities of strong alcoholic drinks (more than 30% alcohol by volume) should be avoided because it may lead to increased dissolution rates of Acme Product and, therefore, may increase the frequency of gastrointestinal adverse reactions.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Vaccination during treatment with Acme Product has not been studied. Immunosuppression is a risk factor for the use of live vaccines. The risk of vaccination should be weighed against the benefit.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">There is no evidence for Acme Product interaction with cytochrome P450 and the most common efflux and uptake transporters, thus no interactions are expected with medicinal products metabolised or transported by these systems (see section 5.2).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                </div>"         ]       ], [

class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Description of selected adverse reactions</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Gastrointestinal disturbances</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Data from the Phase III clinical study as well as from the literature show that gastrointestinal disorders with dimethyl fumarate‑containing products are most likely to occur during the first 2 to 3 months after starting treatment. No apparent dose relationship and no risk factors for the occurrence of these adverse reactions could be identified. Diarrhoea was a common adverse reaction (36.9%) among patients taking Acme Product, leading to medicinal product withdrawal in about 10% of patients. More than 90% of these diarrhoea events were of mild to moderate severity (see section 4.4).</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;text-autospace:none\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Flushing</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Based on observations in the Phase III clinical study as well as on literature data, flushing is most likely to occur during the early weeks of treatment and tends to lessen with time. In the clinical study a total of 20.8% of patients receiving Acme Product </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">experienced flushing, which was mild in the majority of cases (see section 4.4). Published clinical experience with dimethyl fumarate-containing products shows that individual episodes of flushing usually begin shortly after taking the tablets and resolve within a few hours.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Haematological changes</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Data from the Phase III clinical study as well as from the\nliterature show that changes in haematological parameters are most likely to\noccur during the first 3 months after starting treatment with dimethyl\nfumarate. In particular, in the clinical study there was a slight decrease in\nmean lymphocyte counts starting between weeks 3 and 5 and reaching a\nmaximum in week 12 where approximately one third of patients had\nlymphocyte values below 1.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L. The mean and median values of\nlymphocytes remained within the normal range during the clinical study. At week 16\n(end of treatment), there was no further decline in lymphocyte counts. At week\n16\n                                        </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">of treatment</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">, 13/175 (7.4%) </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">of patients were noted to have lymphocyte levels &lt;0.7x 10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L.\nBlood sampling for safety clinical laboratory tests at follow-up visits was\nonly performed in case of abnormalities at the preceeding visit. During the\ntreatment free follow up, lymphocyte levels of &lt;0.7x 10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L were\nobserved in 1/29 (3.5%) patient at 6 months and 0/28 (0%) at 12 months after\nstopping treatment.\n                                        </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">At 12 months after stopping treatment\n3/28 (10.7%) of patients had lymphocyte values below 1.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L,\nwhich would represent 3/279 (1.1%) of the patients started on Acme Product.\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">For the total\nleukocyte count, a decline became apparent at week 12 of treatment; it\nslowly increased again at week 16 (end of treatment); and 12 months\nafter stopping treatment all patients had values above 3.0x10\n                                            <sup>9</sup>/L.\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">A transient increase in mean values of eosinophils was noted as early as week 3, reached a maximum at week 5 and 8, and had returned to baseline values at week 16. </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">For monitoring recommendations and clinical management of haematological adverse reactions, see section 4.4.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                </div>"         ];

           fhir:Narrative.status [ fhir:value "additional" ];
           fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Pharmacotherapeutic group: </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Other immunosuppressants,</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">ATC code: </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">L04AX07</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                </div>"         ];
         fhir:Composition.section.section [
           fhir:index 0;
           fhir:Element.id [ fhir:value "98bc7dbb-bac6-440c-a5f9-a012d496b8ef" ];
           fhir:Composition.section.title [ fhir:value "Mechanism of action" ];
           fhir:Composition.section.code [
             fhir:CodeableConcept.coding [
               fhir:index 0;
               fhir:Coding.system [ fhir:value "http://spor.ema.europa.eu/v1/example-sections" ];
               fhir:Coding.code [ fhir:value "34" ];
               fhir:Coding.display [ fhir:value "Mechanism of action" ]             ]           ];
           fhir:Composition.section.text [
             fhir:Narrative.status [ fhir:value "additional" ];
             fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The anti-inflammatory and immunomodulating effects of dimethyl fumarate and its metabolite monomethyl fumarate are not fully elucidated but are thought to be mainly due to the interaction with the intracellular reduced glutathione of cells directly involved in the pathogenesis of psoriasis. This interaction with glutathione leads to the inhibition of translocation into the nucleus and the transcriptional activity of the nuclear factor kappa‑light‑chain‑enhancer of activated B‑cells (NF‑κB).</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The main activity of dimethyl fumarate and monomethyl fumarate is considered to be immunomodulatory, resulting in a shift in T helper cells (Th) from the Th1 and Th17 profile to a Th2 phenotype. The inflammatory cytokine production is reduced with induction of proapoptotic events, inhibition of keratinocyte proliferation, reduced expression of adhesion molecules, and diminished inflammatory infiltrate within psoriatic plaques.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <u>\n                                                <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                            </u>\n                                        </p>\n                                    </div>"           ]         ], [
           fhir:index 1;
           fhir:Element.id [ fhir:value "287a0ff0-769c-4b91-90b3-83db1a79dd2d" ];
           fhir:Composition.section.title [ fhir:value "Clinical efficacy and safety" ];
           fhir:Composition.section.code [
             fhir:CodeableConcept.coding [
               fhir:index 0;
               fhir:Coding.system [ fhir:value "http://spor.ema.europa.eu/v1/example-sections" ];
               fhir:Coding.code [ fhir:value "36" ];
               fhir:Coding.display [ fhir:value "Clinical efficacy and safety" ]             ]           ];
           fhir:Composition.section.text [
             fhir:Narrative.status [ fhir:value "additional" ];
             fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The safety and efficacy of Acme Product was assessed in one double‑blind, </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">3‑arm, placebo‑ and active comparator-controlled Phase III study (1102) in patients with moderate to severe plaque psoriasis (Study 1102). 704 patients were randomised to receive Acme Product, an active comparator (Fumaderm, a combination product with the same content of </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">dimethyl fumarate plus</span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">3 monoethyl fumarate salts) and placebo in a ratio of 2:2:1. Patients began treatment with tablets containing 30 mg/day </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">dimethyl fumarate</span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">or placebo, titrating up to a maximum of 720 mg/day in both active treatment arms as described in section 4.2. </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">If treatment success was observed before the maximum dose of 720 mg/day of dimethyl fumarate was reached, no further increase of dosage was necessary and the dosage was to be steadily reduced to an individual maintenance dose. In case of individual intolerability of the increased dosage during weeks 4 to 16, the patient was to return to the last tolerated dose taken since the start of week 4, which was to be maintained until end of the treatment period (week 16). </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Patients received treatment for up to 16 weeks and follow-up visits were planned for up to 12 months after treatment was stopped.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The demographic and baseline characteristics were well balanced between the treatment </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">groups</span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">. Of the 699 patients, most were Caucasian (99%) and male (65%), and the mean age was 44 years. Most patients (91%) were &lt;65 years of age. Most patients had moderate psoriasis based on Psoriasis Area and Severity Index (PASI) and Physician’s Global Assessment (PGA) scores at baseline: the mean PASI score at baseline was 16.35 and 60% of patients scored as moderate on the PGA. The majority of patients reported a “very large” or “extremely large” effect of psoriasis on their life based on the Dermatology Life Quality Index (DLQI), with a mean DLQI score of 11.5.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal;text-autospace:none\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <a name=\"_Ref431313822\">\n                                                <span lang=\"EN-GB\">After 16 weeks of treatment, Acme Product was found to be superior to placebo (p&lt;0.0001) based on PASI 75 and PGA score clear or almost clear and non‑inferior (using a non-inferiority margin of ‑15%) to the active comparator (p&lt;0.0003) based on PASI 75. </span>\n                                            </a>\n                                        </p>\n Hence it is reasonable to expect the long-term efficacy of Acme Product to also be comparable to dimethyl fumarate-containing products. Maintenance of long term efficacy has been well described for other dimethyl fumarate-containing products, and therefore</span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">the treatment benefits seen with Acme Product at 16 weeks can be expected to be maintained in patients treated over the long term for at least 24 months.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    </div>"           ]         ], [

After oral administration of a single Acme Product 120 mg tablet in healthy subjects, </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">monomethyl fumarate</span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">reached plasma peak concentrations of around 1325 ng/mL and 1311 ng/mL\nunder fasted or fed conditions, respectively.            fhir:Composition.section.text [
             fhir:Narrative.status [ fhir:value "additional" ];
             fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                        <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal;page-break-after:  avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The biotransformation of dimethyl fumarate does not involve cytochrome P450 isoenzymes.</span>\n                                            <i>In vitro </i>studies have shown that monomethyl fumarate at the therapeutic dose\ndoes not inhibit or induce any of the cytochrome P450 enzymes, it is not a\nsubstrate or inhibitor of P‑glycoprotein and is not an inhibitor of the\nmost common efflux and uptake transporters\n                                            <span style=\"color:#4BA524;  background:white\">. </span>\n                                            <span style=\"color:black;background:white\">In vitro studies have shown that dimethyl fumarate at a therapeutic dose does not inhibit CYP3A4/5 and BCRP and is a weak P-glycoprotein inhibitor.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal\" id=\"8a56455c-0939-4203-b538-47f084199bc9\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                        <i>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">In vitro</span>\n                                        </i>\n                                        <none/>\n                                        <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal\" id=\"8a56455c-0939-4203-b538-47f084199bc9\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">studies have shown that hydrolysis of dimethyl fumarate to </span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">monomethyl fumarate</span>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">occurs rapidly at pH 8 (pH in the small intestine), but not at pH 1 (pH in the stomach). A part of the total dimethyl fumarate is hydrolysed by esterases and the alkaline milieu of the small intestine, while the remainder enters the portal vein blood. Further studies have shown that dimethyl fumarate (and to a lesser extent monomethyl fumarate) reacts partially with reduced glutathione forming a glutathione-adduct. These adducts were detected in animal studies in the intestinal mucosa of rats and to a smaller extent in portal vein blood. Unconjugated dimethyl fumarate, however, cannot be detected in the plasma of animals or psoriatic patients following oral administration. By contrast, unconjugated monomethyl fumarate is detectable in plasma. Further metabolism occurs through oxidation via the tricarboxylic acid cycle forming carbon dioxide and water.</span>\n                                        </p>\n                                        <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                            <u>\n                                                <span lang=\"EN-GB\"/>\n                                            </u>\n                                        </p>\n                                    </div>"           ]         ], [

         fhir:Composition.section.title [ fhir:value "5.3     Preclinical safety data" ];
         fhir:Composition.section.code [
           fhir:CodeableConcept.coding [
             fhir:index 0;
             fhir:Coding.system [ fhir:value "http://spor.ema.europa.eu/v1/example-sections" ];
             fhir:Coding.code [ fhir:value "45" ];
             fhir:Coding.display [ fhir:value "5.3 Preclinical safety data" ]           ]         ];
         fhir:Composition.section.text [
           fhir:Narrative.status [ fhir:value "additional" ];
           fhir:Narrative.div "<div xmlns=\"http://www.w3.org/1999/xhtml\">\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal;page-break-after:  avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Non-clinical safety pharmacology and genotoxicity data reveal no special hazard for humans.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal;page-break-after:  avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Toxicology</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">The kidney was identified as a major target organ of toxicity in\nnon-clinical studies. Renal findings in dogs included minimal to moderate\ntubular hypertrophy, increased incidence and severity of tubular vacuolation\nand minimal to slight tubular degeneration, which were considered\ntoxicologically relevant. The no‑observed adverse-effect-level (NOAEL) after\n3 months of treatment was 30 mg/kg/day, which corresponds to 2.9‑fold\nand 9.5‑fold the human systemic exposure at the highest recommended dose\n(720 mg/day), as AUC and C\n                                            <sub>max</sub>values, respectively.\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal;page-break-after:  avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Reproduction toxicity</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">No fertility or pre- and post-natal development studies have been conducted with Acme Product.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">There were no effects on foetal body weights or malformations attributed to maternal administration of dimethyl fumarate</span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">during the embryo‑foetal development study in rats. However, there\nwas an increased number of foetuses with the variations “supernumerary liver\nlobe” and “abnormal iliac alignment” at maternally toxic doses. The NOAEL for\nmaternal and embryo‑foetal toxicity was 40 mg/kg/day, corresponding\nto 0.2‑fold and 2.0‑fold the human systemic exposure at the highest\nrecommended dose (720 mg/day), as AUC and C\n                                            <sub>max</sub>values, respectively.\n                                        </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Dimethyl fumarate has been shown to cross the placental membrane into foetal blood in rats.</span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"margin-right:-.1pt;line-height:normal;page-break-after:  avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <u>\n                                            <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Carcinogenicity</span>\n                                        </u>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal;page-break-after:avoid\" class=\"MsoNormal\">\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">No carcinogenicity studies have been performed for </span>\n                                        <span lang=\"EN-GB\">Acme Product. Based on available data suggesting that fumaric acid esters may activate cellular pathways related to the development of renal tumours, a potential tumorigenic activity of exogenously administered dimethyl fumarate on the kidneys cannot be excluded. </span>\n                                    </p>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                    <p style=\"line-height:normal\" class=\"MsoNormal\"/>\n                                </div>"         ]       ]     ], [
